### Environment Audit (EA) Rules, 2025

- Pages: 86
- Focus: The framework, tiers, and statutory backing of the newly notified Environment Audit Rules, 2025.
- Question quota hint: 4
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- EA Rules 2025 were developed under the Environment Protection Act (1986).
- EA differs from EIA as EIA is conducted prior to project establishment, while EA checks conformity to the Environmental Management Plan.
- Introduced initially in 1992 under the Environment (Protection) Rules, requiring annual environmental statements to SPCBs.
- Features a Two-Tiered System: Tier-1 (CPCB/SPCB review) and Tier-2 (Environment auditor-based mechanism).
- Environment Audit Designate Agency (EADA) is responsible for certification, registration, and oversight of Environment Auditors.

#### Section Excerpt

MoEFCC notified the Environment Audit (EA) Rules, 2025 under the Environment Protection Act (1986). EA differs from EIA as it determines conformity to an approved Environmental Management Plan post-establishment. It features a Two-Tiered System: Tier-1 (government regulator review by CPCB/SPCB) and Tier-2 (Environment auditor-based). An Environment Audit Designate Agency (EADA) oversees certification and registration of auditors.

#### Claims

- The Environment Audit (EA) Rules, 2025 were notified by the MoEFCC under the Environment Protection Act, 1986.
- Environmental Audit (EA) differs from Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA) as EA is conducted post-establishment to check conformity to an approved Environmental Management Plan, whereas EIA is conducted prior to project establishment.
- The Environment Audit (EA) Rules, 2025 feature a Two-Tiered System comprising a government regulator review by CPCB/SPCB (Tier-1) and an Environment auditor-based mechanism (Tier-2).
- The Environment Audit Designate Agency (EADA) is responsible for the certification, registration, and oversight of Environment Auditors.
- Environmental Auditing was initially introduced in India in 1992 under the Environment (Protection) Rules, requiring the submission of annual environmental statements to State Pollution Control Boards (SPCBs).

### Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA) and Ex-Post Facto Clearance

- Pages: 86
- Focus: Supreme Court rulings on ex-post facto environmental clearance for mining projects.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 2

#### Evidence Bullets

- The Supreme Court overturned its decision that restrained the Centre from granting ex-post facto environmental clearance to mining projects.
- Ex-post facto EC allows a project to continue without having obtained an Environmental Clearance prior to its commencement.

#### Section Excerpt

The Supreme Court reviewed and overturned its May 2025 decision in Vanashakti v. Union of India, which had restrained the Centre from granting ex-post facto environmental clearance (EC) to mining projects or regularising actions contravening the 2006 EIA notification. An ex-post facto EC allows a project proponent to continue without obtaining an EC prior to project commencement.

#### Claims

- An ex-post facto environmental clearance (EC) allows a project to continue operations even if it did not obtain an EC prior to the commencement of the project.
- The Supreme Court overturned its previous decision that had restrained the Centre from granting ex-post facto environmental clearance to mining projects.

## Environmental Clearance and Dam Safety

- Topic: Environmental Governance
- Pages: 87-88
- Rationale: Covers the EC categorization (A vs B), the Great Nicobar Project controversy, and the Dam Safety Act 2021.

### Dam Safety in India and Sedimentation Vulnerabilities

- Pages: 87-88
- Focus: Dam statistics, sedimentation issues, Dam Safety Act 2021, and related national/international initiatives.
- Question quota hint: 4
- Claim count: 7

#### Evidence Bullets

- India is the 3rd largest dam-owning nation (after China and USA), with Maharashtra having the highest number of large dams.
- Indira Sagar Dam (Narmada River, MP) is India's largest reservoir by volume.
- Dam Safety Act, 2021 created a 4-tier institutional framework: NCDS, NDSA, SCDS, and SDSO.
- DRIP Phase II and III are implemented with financial assistance from the World Bank and AIIB.
- National Centre for Earthquake Safety of Dams is located at MNIT Jaipur.
- World Commission on Dams was established by the World Bank and IUCN in 1998.

#### Section Excerpt

India is the 3rd largest dam-owning nation, with Maharashtra having the highest number of large dams and Indira Sagar being the largest by volume. Many reservoirs have lost nearly 50% capacity due to sedimentation. The Dam Safety Act, 2021 established the NCDS, NDSA, SCDS, and SDSO. Initiatives include DRIP (funded by World Bank and AIIB), SHAISYS, DHARMA, and the National Centre for Earthquake Safety of Dams at MNIT Jaipur.

#### Claims

- India is the third largest dam-owning nation globally, following China and the USA.
- Maharashtra has the highest number of large dams among all Indian states.
- Indira Sagar Dam, located on the Narmada River in Madhya Pradesh, is India's largest reservoir by volume.
- The Dam Safety Act, 2021 established a four-tier institutional framework comprising the NCDS, NDSA, SCDS, and SDSO.
- The Dam Rehabilitation and Improvement Project (DRIP) Phase II and III are implemented with financial assistance from the World Bank and the Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB).
- The National Centre for Earthquake Safety of Dams is located at MNIT Jaipur.
- The World Commission on Dams was established by the World Bank and the International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN) in 1998.

### Environmental Clearance (EC) in India

- Pages: 87
- Focus: EIA Notification 2006, project categorization, and Supreme Court rulings on ex post facto clearance.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- EIA Notification 2006 lists over 39 activities requiring prior EC.
- Category A projects are handled by MoEF&CC at the Central level.
- Category B projects are handled by SEIAA at the State level.
- Supreme Court held in Common Cause v. UoI (2017) that ex post facto environmental clearance is invalid.

#### Section Excerpt

EC is required for projects significantly impacting the environment under the EIA Notification, 2006. Projects are categorized into Category A (Central level, MoEF&CC) and Category B (State level, SEIAA). Prior clearance is mandatory, and the Supreme Court (Common Cause v. UoI, 2017) ruled that ex post facto or retrospective clearance is alien to environmental jurisprudence.

#### Claims

- Under the EIA Notification 2006, Category A projects are handled by the MoEF&CC at the Central level, while Category B projects are handled by the SEIAA at the State level.
- The Supreme Court ruled in the Common Cause v. UoI (2017) case that ex post facto or retrospective environmental clearance is invalid and alien to environmental jurisprudence.
- The EIA Notification 2006 mandates prior Environmental Clearance for over 39 listed activities.

### Great Nicobar Island Project (GNIP) and Tribal Rights

- Pages: 87
- Focus: Infrastructure project components, nodal agencies, and the conflict between PAT 1956 and FRA 2006 regarding tribal rights.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Tribal Councils in A&N Islands have limited advisory/executive powers, unlike Sixth Schedule autonomous councils.
- PAT 1956 allows unilateral forest land diversion, conflicting with FRA 2006's mandate for Gram Sabha consent.
- GNIP was conceived by NITI Aayog; ANIIDCO is the nodal agency.
- Project includes an International Transshipment Port at Galathea Bay.
- Galathea Bay is a Ramsar Site and a key nesting site for the endangered Leatherback Sea Turtle.

#### Section Excerpt

The GNIP is a massive Greenfield infrastructure project conceived by NITI Aayog, with ANIIDCO as the nodal agency. It includes a transshipment port at Galathea Bay, an airport, a power plant, and a township. A conflict exists over forest land diversion, with the administration citing the Protection of Aboriginal Tribes Act, 1956 (PAT) to bypass the Forest Rights Act, 2006 (FRA) which mandates Gram Sabha consent. Galathea Bay is a Ramsar Site and nesting site for the Leatherback Sea Turtle.

#### Claims

- The Great Nicobar Island Project (GNIP) was conceived by NITI Aayog, with the Andaman and Nicobar Islands Integrated Development Corporation (ANIIDCO) serving as its nodal agency.
- The administration in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands has cited the Protection of Aboriginal Tribes Act, 1956 (PAT) to bypass the Forest Rights Act, 2006 (FRA) mandate requiring Gram Sabha consent for forest land diversion.
- Galathea Bay, the proposed site for the GNIP transshipment port, is a Ramsar Site and a key nesting site for the endangered Leatherback Sea Turtle.
- Tribal Councils in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands have limited advisory and executive powers, unlike the autonomous councils established under the Sixth Schedule of the Constitution.

### Seed Management and Draft Seeds Bill, 2025

- Pages: 88
- Focus: Key provisions of the Draft Seeds Bill, 2025, including mandatory registration and the SATHI portal.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Draft Seeds Bill, 2025 replaces the Seeds Act, 1966, and Seeds (Control) Order, 1983.
- Un-registered seeds cannot be sold, except for farmers' varieties and seeds produced exclusively for export.
- SATHI portal (MoAFW + NIC) ensures complete traceability of seeds from origin to farmer.
- Seed varieties must conform to the Indian Minimum Seed Certification Standards.

#### Section Excerpt

The Draft Seeds Bill, 2025 seeks to replace the Seeds Act, 1966, and Seeds (Control) Order, 1983 to regulate seed quality. It mandates that no unregistered seed can be sold, excepting farmers' varieties and export-only seeds. It requires mandatory onboarding on the SATHI portal (created by MoAFW and NIC) for complete seed traceability. Central and State Seed Committees will be constituted.

#### Claims

- The Draft Seeds Bill, 2025 seeks to replace the Seeds Act, 1966, and the Seeds (Control) Order, 1983.
- Under the Draft Seeds Bill, 2025, the sale of unregistered seeds is prohibited, except for farmers' varieties and seeds produced exclusively for export.
- The SATHI portal, created by MoAFW and NIC, is mandated for complete seed traceability from origin to farmer.
- The Draft Seeds Bill, 2025 mandates the constitution of both Central and State Seed Committees.
- Seed varieties must conform to the Indian Minimum Seed Certification Standards under the Draft Seeds Bill, 2025.

## Draft Seeds Bill and Sand Mining

- Topic: Agriculture and Mining
- Pages: 89-90
- Rationale: Compares the 1966 Seeds Act with the 2025 Bill and details the legal prerequisites for sand mining replenishment.

### Draft Seeds Bill 2025 and India's Seed Sector

- Pages: 89-90
- Focus: Provisions of the Draft Seeds Bill 2025, comparison with the 1966 Act, classification of seeds, and government initiatives.
- Question quota hint: 4
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Draft Seeds Bill 2025 mandates registration for every seed variety before trade and incorporates biotech norms.
- Farmers can save, use, exchange, or sell their seeds without brand registration, but cannot sell under a brand name.
- Breeder Seed is the progeny of the nucleus seed; Foundation Seed is the progeny of breeder seed; Certified Seed is the progeny of foundation seed.
- Odisha launched a roadmap to integrate Landraces (genetically diverse crop populations evolved with traditional practices) into formal seed systems.
- Seed Village Programme (Beej Gram Yojana) aims to improve farmers' saved seed quality.

#### Section Excerpt

Comparative Analysis of Seeds Act, 1966 and Draft Seeds Bill, 2025... Mandatory registration for every seed variety before trade... Farmers can save, exchange, and sell their seeds... Overview of India's Seed Sector: 5th largest Seed Industry... Recognizes three generations of seeds: Breeder Seed, Foundation Seed, Certified Seed... Key Initiatives: Protection of Plant Varieties and Farmers' Rights Act, 2001... Seed Village Programme... Landraces are genetically diverse crop populations...

#### Claims

- The Draft Seeds Bill 2025 mandates the registration of every seed variety before it can be traded.
- Under the Draft Seeds Bill 2025, farmers are allowed to save, use, exchange, or sell their seeds without brand registration, provided they do not sell them under a brand name.
- In India's seed sector, Foundation Seed is the progeny of Breeder Seed, and Certified Seed is the progeny of Foundation Seed.
- Landraces are genetically diverse crop populations that have evolved through traditional farming practices.
- The Seed Village Programme (Beej Gram Yojana) is designed to improve the quality of seeds saved by farmers.

### Sand Mining and Environmental Regulations

- Pages: 90
- Focus: Supreme Court rulings, environmental impacts, and the legal framework governing sand mining in India.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Supreme Court ruled that a replenishment study is a mandatory prerequisite for environmental clearance for sand mining.
- Deepak Kumar vs State of Haryana (2012) made environmental clearance mandatory for all minor mineral extractions, including sand.
- EIA Notification (2016 Amendment) introduced cluster-based assessments and made replenishment studies a key part of the District Survey Report (DSR).
- Unrestricted sand mining causes riverbank erosion, lowers groundwater tables, and increases flood risks.

#### Section Excerpt

Supreme Court (SC) observed that replenishment data is a mandatory prerequisite for environmental clearance in addition to District Survey Report (DSR)... Deepak Kumar vs State of Haryana (2012): SC made environmental clearance mandatory for all minor mineral extractions, including sand... EIA Notification (2016 Amendment): Cluster-based assessments and making replenishment studies a key part of DSR.

#### Claims

- Replenishment data is a mandatory prerequisite, in addition to the District Survey Report (DSR), for obtaining environmental clearance for sand mining.
- The Supreme Court judgment in Deepak Kumar vs State of Haryana (2012) made environmental clearance mandatory for all minor mineral extractions, including sand.
- The EIA Notification (2016 Amendment) introduced cluster-based assessments and integrated replenishment studies into the District Survey Report (DSR).
- Unrestricted sand mining causes ecological damage such as riverbank erosion, lowering of groundwater tables, and increased flood risks.

### Uniform Renewable Energy Tariff (URET)

- Pages: 91
- Focus: The scrapping of URET by the Ministry of Power and its implications.
- Question quota hint: 1
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- URET was scrapped by the Ministry of Power.
- It aimed to average competitive bid tariffs of similar RE projects to provide a uniform tariff.
- It was revoked because procurers were reluctant to sign Power Sale Agreements due to tariff uncertainty over a three-year fixed period.

#### Section Excerpt

Uniform Renewable Energy Tariff (URET) scrapped by Ministry of Power. Aims to provide uniform tariff to consumers by averaging competitive bid tariffs of similar renewable energy projects within central pools. Reasons for revocation: Procurers were reluctant to sign Power Sale Agreements due to uncertainty of tariffs over the three-year fixed period causing stalled projects.

#### Claims

- The Uniform Renewable Energy Tariff (URET) was scrapped by the Ministry of Power.
- The Uniform Renewable Energy Tariff (URET) aimed to provide a uniform tariff to consumers by averaging competitive bid tariffs of similar renewable energy projects within central pools.
- The URET was revoked because procurers were reluctant to sign Power Sale Agreements due to tariff uncertainty over a three-year fixed period, which caused stalled projects.

### Green Municipal Bonds (GMB)

- Pages: 92
- Focus: India's first certified GMB by Ghaziabad Nagar Nigam and municipal bond basics.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Ghaziabad Nagar Nigam issued India's first certified Green Municipal Bond.
- The funds raised were used for a Tertiary Sewage Treatment Plant under the PPP-HAM model.
- Municipal bonds are non-convertible debt securities issued by bodies entrusted with functions under Article 243W of the Constitution.

#### Section Excerpt

Ghaziabad Nagar Nigam pioneered India's first certified GMB issued under Swachh Bharat Mission-Urban, raising ₹150 crore for development of Tertiary Sewage Treatment Plant (TSTP). TSTP was developed under Public-Private Hybrid Annuity Model (PPP-HAM). Municipal bonds refer to non-convertible debt securities issued by municipal body or others established for such purposes and entrusted with functions under Article 243W of Constitution. Green bonds are used to raise funds specifically for climate mitigation, adaptation and other environment friendly projects.

#### Claims

- Ghaziabad Nagar Nigam issued India's first certified Green Municipal Bond (GMB).
- Municipal bonds are non-convertible debt securities issued by bodies entrusted with functions under Article 243W of the Constitution.
- Green bonds are financial instruments used to raise funds specifically for climate mitigation, adaptation, and other environment-friendly projects.
- The Tertiary Sewage Treatment Plant (TSTP) funded by the Ghaziabad Green Municipal Bond was developed under the Public-Private Hybrid Annuity Model (PPP-HAM).

### Renewable Purchase Obligation (RPO) and Renewable Consumption Obligation (RCO)

- Pages: 92
- Focus: Transition from RPO to RCO under the Energy Conservation Act 2001.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- RCO draft notification was issued under the Energy Conservation Act (ECA) 2001.
- RPO was established under the Electricity Act, 2003.
- RPO focuses on the purchase of electricity from RE sources, whereas RCO focuses on actual consumption.
- Penalties for non-compliance with RCO are overseen by the Bureau of Energy Efficiency (BEE).

#### Section Excerpt

Ministry of Power issued a revised draft notification on RCO under Energy Conservation Act (ECA) 2001 establishing mandatory year-wise Renewable Energy (RE) consumption targets from 2024-25 to 2029-30. RPO, established under Electricity Act, 2003, mandates electricity distribution companies, captive power producers and open-access consumers to annually purchase a certain minimum amount of RE. While RPO focuses on actual purchase, RCO focuses on actual consumption from RE sources. Creates binding obligations with penalties for non-compliance overseen by Bureau of Energy Efficiency (BEE).

#### Claims

- The Renewable Consumption Obligation (RCO) is established under the Energy Conservation Act (ECA) 2001.
- The Renewable Purchase Obligation (RPO) is established under the Electricity Act, 2003.
- The Renewable Purchase Obligation (RPO) focuses on the actual purchase of renewable energy, whereas the Renewable Consumption Obligation (RCO) focuses on the actual consumption from renewable energy sources.
- Penalties for non-compliance with the Renewable Consumption Obligation (RCO) are overseen by the Bureau of Energy Efficiency (BEE).

### Sustainable Aviation Fuel (SAF)

- Pages: 92
- Focus: SAF blending mandates, feedstocks, and the Indian Oil-Air India MoU.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Indian Oil and Air India signed an MoU for the supply of Sustainable Aviation Fuel (SAF).
- SAF can be blended up to 50% in conventional aviation turbine fuel.
- India has mandated a 1% SAF blending in jet fuel for international airlines starting in 2027.
- SAF is produced from non-petroleum feedstocks like corn grain, algae, and agricultural residues.

#### Section Excerpt

Indian Oil signed a MoU with Air India for supply of sustainable aviation fuel. An alternative fuel made from non-petroleum feedstocks that reduces emissions from air transportation. Can be blended up to 50% in conventional aviation turbine fuel (ATF or jet fuel). India mandated 1% SAF blending in jet fuel sold to international airlines from 2027. Raw material: Corn grain, Oil seeds, Algae, Agricultural residues, Forestry residues, Wastewater treatment sludge etc.

#### Claims

- Sustainable Aviation Fuel (SAF) can be blended up to 50% with conventional aviation turbine fuel.
- India has mandated a 1% Sustainable Aviation Fuel (SAF) blending in jet fuel for international airlines starting in 2027.
- Sustainable Aviation Fuel (SAF) is produced from non-petroleum feedstocks, including algae, agricultural residues, and wastewater treatment sludge.

## Gas Hydrates and IEA

- Topic: Energy and Organizations
- Pages: 93-94
- Rationale: Details the nature of gas hydrates and the membership criteria/reports of the International Energy Agency.

### Gas Hydrates

- Pages: 93
- Focus: Characteristics, locations, and significance of gas hydrates as an unconventional hydrocarbon source.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Gas hydrates are crystalline solids composed of water and gas that contain large amounts of methane.
- They are classified as unconventional hydrocarbons requiring advanced and non-traditional extraction technologies.
- Found in marine sediments directly below the sea floor and within the Arctic permafrost layer.
- In India, significant quantities are located around the Andaman Islands and in the Krishna-Godavari offshore basin.
- China is building the world's first permanent undersea research station to study gas hydrates.

#### Section Excerpt

Gas hydrates are crystalline solids composed of water and gas, containing large amounts of methane. They are classified as unconventional hydrocarbons because extracting them requires advanced technologies. They exist in huge quantities in marine sediments below the sea floor and within the permafrost layer in the Arctic. In India, huge quantities are found around the Andaman Islands and in Krishna-Godavari offshore. China is constructing the world's first permanent undersea research station to study them.

#### Claims

- Gas hydrates are crystalline solids composed of water and gas that contain large amounts of methane.
- Gas hydrates are classified as unconventional hydrocarbons because their extraction requires advanced, non-traditional technologies.
- Globally, gas hydrates are found in marine sediments below the sea floor and within the Arctic permafrost layer.
- In India, significant quantities of gas hydrates are located around the Andaman Islands and in the Krishna-Godavari offshore basin.
- China is constructing the world's first permanent undersea research station to study gas hydrates.

### International Energy Agency (IEA)

- Pages: 93
- Focus: Genesis, membership criteria, and flagship reports of the International Energy Agency.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 6

#### Evidence Bullets

- IEA was founded in 1974 to ensure the security of oil supplies and is headquartered in Paris, France.
- India is an associate member of the IEA, not a full member.
- Full membership requires OECD membership, accessible crude oil reserves equivalent to 90 days of the previous year's net imports, and a 10% demand restraint programme.
- Flagship publications include the World Energy Outlook.
- Recent reports include the Global Methane Tracker 2025, Delivering Sustainable Fuels, and Global EV Outlook 2025.

#### Section Excerpt

The International Energy Agency (IEA), located in Paris, France, was founded in 1974 to ensure the security of oil supplies. It has 32 Member countries and 13 Association countries, with India being an associate member. To be a full member, a country must be an OECD member, maintain crude oil reserves equivalent to 90 days of the previous year's net imports, and have a demand restraint programme to reduce oil consumption by up to 10%. Flagship publications include the World Energy Outlook, Global Methane Tracker, Delivering Sustainable Fuels, and Global EV Outlook.

#### Claims

- The International Energy Agency (IEA) was founded in 1974 with the primary mandate of ensuring the security of oil supplies.
- India is an associate member of the International Energy Agency (IEA), not a full member.
- A country must be a member of the OECD to be eligible for full membership in the International Energy Agency (IEA).
- IEA full membership requires a country to maintain crude oil reserves equivalent to 90 days of its previous year's net imports.
- To become a full member of the IEA, a country must have a demand restraint programme capable of reducing national oil consumption by up to 10%.
- The World Energy Outlook, Global Methane Tracker, and Global EV Outlook are flagship publications of the International Energy Agency (IEA).

Its purpose is to improve food security in semi-arid regions and support smallholder farmers in drylands globally. Key achievements include being awarded the Africa Food Prize in 2021 and developing the world's first pigeon pea hybrid. Recently, ICRISAT collaborated with RIS to launch the ICRISAT Centre of Excellence for South-South Cooperation.

### Solar Energy Corporation of India (SECI)

- Pages: 94
- Focus: Status, functions, and achievements of SECI in India's renewable energy sector.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- SECI is a Navratna Central Public Sector Undertaking under the Ministry of New and Renewable Energy (MNRE).
- Established in 2011 specifically for the implementation of the National Solar Mission.
- Functions as a Category-I (highest) power trading licensee under the Central Electricity Regulatory Commission (CERC).
- Implements special regional models such as the greening of islands (Lakshadweep, A&N) and a proposed 5 GW high-altitude grid-linked capacity in Ladakh.

#### Section Excerpt

Established in 2011 for the implementation of the National Solar Mission, SECI is a Navratna Central Public Sector Undertaking under the Ministry of New and Renewable Energy (MNRE). It is the designated Renewable Energy Implementing Agency (REIA) for MNRE schemes and functions as a Category-I power trading licensee under CERC. SECI implements special programmes like the greening of islands (Lakshadweep, A&N Islands) and high-altitude grid-linked capacity in Ladakh.

#### Claims

- SECI functions as a Category-I power trading licensee under the Central Electricity Regulatory Commission (CERC).
- SECI is responsible for implementing special regional renewable energy models, including the greening of islands like Lakshadweep and Andaman & Nicobar, and high-altitude grid-linked capacity in Ladakh.

### Disaster Risk Reduction (DRR) Financing and UNDRR

- Pages: 96
- Focus: India's DRR financing under the 15th Finance Commission, Sendai Framework, and UNDRR's role.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- UNDRR released the Global Assessment Report (GAR) titled Resilience Pays.
- 15th Finance Commission recommended the creation of National and State Disaster Mitigation Funds (NDMF and SDMF).
- Centre contributes 75% to SDMF for general states and 90% for North-Eastern/Himalayan states.
- Sendai Framework for DRR (2015-30) is the successor to the Hyogo Framework for Action.
- UNDRR, headquartered in Geneva, is the lead UN agency for coordinating DRR and achieving Sendai Framework goals.

#### Section Excerpt

UNDRR released the Global Assessment Report titled Resilience Pays. India's DRR financing under the 15th Finance Commission exceeds INR 2.32 trillion, using a new methodology based on a Disaster Risk Index. It recommended the creation of NDMF and SDMF, with the Centre contributing 75% for general states and 90% for NE/Himalayan states. The Sendai Framework (2015-30) succeeded the Hyogo Framework.

#### Claims

- The Global Assessment Report (GAR) titled 'Resilience Pays' is released by the United Nations Office for Disaster Risk Reduction (UNDRR).
- The 15th Finance Commission recommended the creation of the National Disaster Mitigation Fund (NDMF) and State Disaster Mitigation Fund (SDMF).
- The Central Government contributes 75% to the State Disaster Mitigation Fund (SDMF) for general category states and 90% for North-Eastern and Himalayan states.
- The Sendai Framework for Disaster Risk Reduction (2015-2030) is the successor to the Hyogo Framework for Action.
- The UNDRR is headquartered in Geneva and is the lead UN agency for coordinating disaster risk reduction and achieving the Sendai Framework goals.

## Cloudbursts and Tsunami Guidelines

- Topic: Disasters
- Pages: 97-98
- Rationale: Explains the IMD criteria for cloudbursts and the NDMA guidelines for tsunami mitigation and oil spill hazards.

### Glacial Lakes and Glacial Lake Outburst Floods (GLOFs)

- Pages: 97-98
- Focus: Types of glacial lakes, causes of GLOFs, and India's monitoring and mitigation strategies.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Supraglacial lakes form in depressions on glaciers, while moraine-dammed lakes form at glacier toes and are highly prone to sudden failure.
- GLOFs can be triggered by glacial surging (rapid short-term advance of a glacier), moraine dam failure, seismic activities, and human activities.
- The Central Water Commission (CWC) monitors 902 glacial lakes and water bodies in the Himalayas.
- The National GLOF Risk Mitigation Project (NGRMP) covers the states of Arunachal Pradesh, Himachal Pradesh, Sikkim, and Uttarakhand.
- Synthetic Aperture Radar imagery is utilized to automatically detect changes in the size of glacial lakes.

#### Section Excerpt

Glacial lakes: Water formed by melting glaciers, usually at or near glacier's base. Two primary types: Supraglacial lakes (Formed by meltwater in depressions on glaciers) and Moraine-dammed lakes (Formed by meltwater at glacier toes, dammed by loose debris or ice-cores, prone to sudden failure). GLOFs: Flood resulting from sudden and rapid release of water from a glacial lake. Major Causes: Glacial Surging, Moraine Dam Failure, Seismic Activities. Central Water Commission (CWC) monitors 902 glacial lakes and water bodies in the Himalayas. National Glacial Lake Outburst Flood (GLOF) Risk Mitigation Project (NGRMP): In Arunachal Pradesh, Himachal Pradesh, Sikkim and Uttarakhand.

#### Claims

- Supraglacial lakes form in depressions on glaciers, whereas moraine-dammed lakes form at glacier toes and are highly prone to sudden failure.
- Glacial Lake Outburst Floods (GLOFs) can be triggered by glacial surging, moraine dam failure, seismic activities, and human activities.
- The Central Water Commission (CWC) monitors glacial lakes and water bodies in the Himalayas.
- The National GLOF Risk Mitigation Project (NGRMP) covers the states of Arunachal Pradesh, Himachal Pradesh, Sikkim, and Uttarakhand.
- Synthetic Aperture Radar (SAR) imagery is utilized to automatically detect changes in the size of glacial lakes.

### Cloudbursts and Orographic Lifting

- Pages: 97
- Focus: Definition, meteorological mechanisms (orographic lift), and disaster risk reduction strategies for cloudbursts.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- The IMD defines a cloudburst as an event where 10 cm of rainfall is received at a station in one hour.
- Cloudbursts are more common in mountainous zones due to orographic lift, where moist air is forced to rise, cooling and condensing rapidly.
- A violent upward flow of air prevents condensing raindrops from falling until the lack of upward air causes the whole stored water to fall at once.
- Climate change exacerbates cloudbursts, as every 1°C rise in temperature allows the air to hold approximately 7% more moisture.

#### Section Excerpt

Extreme precipitation in a short period, sometimes accompanied by hail/thunder, creating flood conditions. Occurs in plains as well, but more common in mountainous zones, due to orographic lift. India Meteorological Department (IMD) terms a rain event as cloud burst if 10 cm rainfall is received at a station in one hour. Challenges with Tackling: Climate Change (E.g., every 1°C rise lets air hold ~7% more moisture). Measures: Cloudburst Disaster Risk Reduction (DRR) Strategy – National Disaster Management Plan (2019) including Landslide Hazard Zonation (LHZ).

#### Claims

- The India Meteorological Department (IMD) defines a cloudburst as an event where 10 cm of rainfall is received at a station in one hour.
- Cloudbursts are more common in mountainous zones than in plains due to orographic lift, which forces moist air to rise, cool, and condense rapidly.
- During a cloudburst, a violent upward flow of air prevents condensing raindrops from falling until the updraft weakens, causing the stored water to fall simultaneously.
- Climate change exacerbates cloudbursts because every 1 degree Celsius rise in temperature allows the air to hold approximately 7% more moisture.

### Oil Spills and Marine Pollution Frameworks

- Pages: 98
- Focus: Hazards of chemical spills (Calcium Carbide), impacts of oil spills, and national/global regulatory frameworks.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Calcium carbide reacts violently with seawater to produce highly flammable acetylene gas and is banned for fruit ripening in India under FSSAI regulations.
- The Indian Coast Guard acts as the nodal agency coordinating oil spill responses under the National Oil Spill Disaster Contingency Plan (1996).
- The Merchant Shipping Act (1958) adopts MARPOL conventions for comprehensive maritime governance and pollution control in India.
- The BUNKER Convention (2001) holds shipowners liable for bunker oil pollution and mandates compulsory insurance coverage.
- Oil spills negatively impact benthic organisms like clams and mussels and poison algae, which disrupts marine food chains.

#### Section Excerpt

Calcium Carbide: A hazardous chemical that reacts violently with seawater to produce highly flammable acetylene gas. Use of calcium carbide for ripening fruits has been banned under Food Safety and Standards Regulations, 2011. Key Framework on Oil Spills: Merchant Shipping Act (1958) adopts MARPOL conventions. National Oil Spill Disaster Contingency Plan (1996): Indian Coast Guard coordinates oil spill response in India's maritime zones as a nodal agency. GLOBAL: MARPOL (1973): International convention preventing marine pollution from ships. BUNKER Convention (2001): Holds shipowners liable for bunker oil pollution. Impact: Poisons algae, disrupting food chains; Affect benthic organisms. E.g., clams and mussels.

#### Claims

- Calcium carbide reacts violently with seawater to produce highly flammable acetylene gas and is banned for fruit ripening in India under Food Safety and Standards Regulations, 2011.
- The Indian Coast Guard is the nodal agency responsible for coordinating oil spill responses in India's maritime zones under the National Oil Spill Disaster Contingency Plan (1996).
- The Merchant Shipping Act (1958) adopts the MARPOL conventions for maritime governance and marine pollution control in India.
- The BUNKER Convention (2001) holds shipowners strictly liable for pollution damage caused by bunker oil and mandates compulsory insurance coverage.
- Oil spills disrupt marine food chains by poisoning algae and negatively impacting benthic organisms such as clams and mussels.

### Tsunamis and NDMA Guidelines

- Pages: 98
- Focus: Causes of tsunamis, wave characteristics (wavelength, amplitude, shoaling), and NDMA mitigation guidelines.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Tsunamis can be caused by earthquakes, landslides, volcanic eruptions, meteorites, and underwater explosions.
- The speed and wavelength of a tsunami primarily depend on ocean depth rather than the distance from the wave's source.
- In deep oceans, tsunami wave amplitude is negligible and often goes unnoticed by ships.
- As tsunami waves approach shallow coastal waters, their wavelength decreases due to shoaling, and their wave amplitude increases significantly.
- NDMA guidelines recommend developing natural buffers such as bio-shields and mangrove regeneration to mitigate tsunami impacts.

#### Section Excerpt

Series of extremely long waves caused by large and sudden displacement of ocean, usually result of an earthquake below or near ocean floor. Causes: Earthquakes, landslides, volcanic eruptions, meteorites, underwater explosions. Wavelength: Speed & wavelength primarily depends on ocean depth, not distance from wave's source. Wavelength in deep ocean is ~200 km and reduces to less than 20 km near coast due to shoaling. Wave Height (Amplitude): Not noticed by ships in deep oceans because their amplitude is negligible. When it approach shallow water, wave amplitude increases. NDMA Guidelines for Tsunami: Mandate a multi-tiered institutional structure... Developing Natural buffers like bio shields, mangrove regeneration etc.

#### Claims

- Tsunamis are caused by large and sudden displacements of the ocean, which can result from earthquakes, landslides, volcanic eruptions, meteorites, and underwater explosions.
- The speed and wavelength of a tsunami primarily depend on the ocean depth rather than the distance from the wave's source.
- In deep oceans, tsunami waves have a negligible amplitude and often go unnoticed by ships, despite having a long wavelength of approximately 200 km.
- As tsunami waves approach shallow coastal waters, their wavelength decreases and their wave amplitude increases significantly due to a process called shoaling.
- NDMA guidelines for tsunamis recommend the development of natural buffers, such as bio-shields and mangrove regeneration, to mitigate impacts.

## Oil Spill Technologies and Alert Systems

- Pages: 99-100

### Disaster Alert Systems (SACHET, Cell Broadcast, EW4All)

- Pages: 100
- Focus: National and global disaster early warning and alert systems.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- SACHET is an SMS-based alert system operationalized by NDMA and developed by C-DOT using the Common Alerting Protocol.
- Cell Broadcast alerts are faster than SMS and are broadcast directly to all mobile phones in an affected area.
- Early Warnings for All (EW4All) was launched at COP27 in 2022 to ensure universal protection by 2027.
- EW4All is jointly led by WMO, UNDRR, ITU, and IFRC.

#### Section Excerpt

SACHET (India's SMS-Based Alert System): Operationalized by National Disaster Management Authority (NDMA). Developed by Centre of Development of Telematics C-DOT using the Common Alerting Protocol (CAP)... Cell Broadcast (Near Real-Time Emergency Alerts): Being developed by C-DOT, CB alerts are broadcast directly to all mobile phones in affected area... Early Warnings for All (EW4All): Aim: Ensure universal protection... by 2027. Launched: At COP27 of UNFCCC in 2022... Jointly led by WMO, UNDRR, ITU and IFRC.

#### Claims

- SACHET is an SMS-based disaster alert system operationalized by the National Disaster Management Authority (NDMA).
- The SACHET alert system was developed by the Centre for Development of Telematics (C-DOT) utilizing the Common Alerting Protocol (CAP).
- Cell Broadcast alerts are faster than traditional SMS and are broadcast directly to all mobile phones within a specific affected area.
- The Early Warnings for All (EW4All) initiative was launched at the UNFCCC COP27 in 2022 with the goal of ensuring universal protection by 2027.
- The Early Warnings for All (EW4All) initiative is jointly led by the WMO, UNDRR, ITU, and IFRC.

### Terms/Concepts in News (Twister, Grey Rhino, Super Typhoon)

- Pages: 100
- Focus: Definitions of specific disaster-related meteorological and conceptual terms.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Twisters form when moist, warm air collides with dry, cold air, creating atmospheric instability and strong updrafts.
- A Grey Rhino event is a highly probable, high-impact, but neglected systemic disruption, unlike random Black Swan events.
- A Super Typhoon is a tropical cyclone with maximum wind speeds exceeding 185 kph.

#### Section Excerpt

TWISTER: Violently spinning (250 Miles/Hr), funnel-shaped columns of air stretching from dark thunderclouds to ground... Develop when moist and warm air collides with dry and cold air... GREY RHINO EVENT: Defined as highly probable, high impact but yet neglected systemic disruptions. These are not random surprises (like Black Swan events)... SUPER TYPHOON: Tropical cyclone with maximum wind speed exceeding 185 kph or more than 100 knots.

#### Claims

- Twisters develop when moist, warm air collides with dry, cold air, creating atmospheric instability and strong updrafts.
- A Grey Rhino event is defined as a highly probable, high-impact systemic disruption that is neglected, which differentiates it from unpredictable Black Swan events.
- A tropical cyclone is classified as a Super Typhoon when its maximum wind speed exceeds 185 kph or more than 100 knots.

### Weather Derivatives (WD)

- Pages: 99-100
- Focus: Launch, mechanism, and utility of Weather Derivatives in India.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- India's first Weather Derivatives are being launched by NCDEX in partnership with IMD.
- They utilize meteorological parameters like rainfall and temperature as underlying assets, unlike traditional financial derivatives.
- They help farmers and allied sectors hedge against risks like irregular rainfall and heatwaves.

#### Section Excerpt

India is to launch its first WD, with National Commodity and Derivatives Exchange Ltd (NCDEX) partnering with India Meteorological Department (IMD) to develop rainfall-based derivative products. It will help farmers and allied sectors hedge against risks like irregular rainfall, heatwaves, etc. Unlike traditional derivatives based on financial assets, WD utilise meteorological parameters, like rainfall and temperature, as underlying asset, tied to a predefined weather index.

#### Claims

- India's first Weather Derivatives are being developed by the National Commodity and Derivatives Exchange Ltd (NCDEX) in partnership with the India Meteorological Department (IMD).
- Unlike traditional financial derivatives, Weather Derivatives utilize meteorological parameters such as rainfall and temperature as their underlying assets.
- Weather Derivatives are utilized to help farmers and allied sectors hedge against financial risks caused by irregular weather events like heatwaves and irregular rainfall.

### Key Technologies to Clean Oil Spills

- Pages: 99
- Focus: Methods and technologies used for oil spill remediation.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Oilzapper and Oilivorous-S are bioremediation technologies developed by TERI that use bacteria to convert hydrocarbons into carbon dioxide and water.
- Milkweed plant fiber can be effectively used as a sorbent material for oil spills.
- Oil booms physically isolate spills, while skimmers scrape oil from the water surface.

#### Section Excerpt

Bioremediation: E.g., Oilzapper & Oilivorous-S, developed by The Energy and Resources Institute (TERI); use bacteria to convert harmful hydrocarbons into harmless carbon dioxide and water. Sorbents: E.g., Milkweed plant's fiber, commonly found in Rajasthan, can be effectively used as a sorbent material. Oil Boom: Involves using large floating booms with skirts extending into the water to physically isolate the spill area. Skimmers: These machines scrape oil from the water surface.

#### Claims

- Oilzapper and Oilivorous-S are bioremediation technologies developed by The Energy and Resources Institute (TERI) that use bacteria to convert harmful hydrocarbons into carbon dioxide and water.
- Milkweed plant fiber, commonly found in Rajasthan, acts as an effective sorbent material for cleaning oil spills.
- In oil spill management, oil booms physically isolate the spill area using floating barriers, whereas skimmers are machines that scrape the oil from the water surface.

Membership: 22 member states and 26 collaborating states. Operates from its regional early warning centre at Asian Institute of Technology in Thailand.

### Miscellaneous Disaster and Weather Phenomena

- Pages: 101
- Focus: Definitions and characteristics of Earthquake Swarms, Swell Waves, Blowouts, and Mesoscale Convective Systems.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Earthquake swarms are sequences of many earthquakes occurring in a short period without a specific main shock.
- Swell waves, also known as Kallakkadal waves in India, are long-wavelength ocean waves largely unaffected by local winds.
- A blowout is an uncontrolled release of gas or oil from a well due to underground pressure or valve failure.
- A Mesoscale Convective System (MCS) is a collection of thunderstorms acting as a system that can last over 12 hours.

#### Section Excerpt

Earthquake Swarm: Sequences of many earthquakes that occur in a relatively short period without a specific main shock. Swell Waves: Long-wavelength ocean waves travelling long distances away from their origin. Largely unaffected by local winds and often go undetected by satellites... Also called Kallakkadal waves in India. Blowout: Oil/gas well accident where underground pressure forces gas/oil to surface uncontrollably. Mesoscale Convective System (MCS): Collection of thunderstorms that act as a system. Can spread across entire state and last >12 hours.

#### Claims

- An earthquake swarm is a sequence of multiple earthquakes occurring in a short timeframe without a distinct main shock.
- Swell waves, also referred to as Kallakkadal waves in India, are long-wavelength ocean waves that remain largely unaffected by local winds.
- A blowout is an industrial accident in an oil or gas well caused by underground pressure forcing hydrocarbons to the surface uncontrollably.
- A Mesoscale Convective System (MCS) is a large collection of thunderstorms that act together as a system and can persist for over 12 hours.

### Tropical Cyclones

- Pages: 101
- Focus: Formation conditions and regional terminology of tropical cyclones.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Tropical cyclones require sea surface temperatures greater than 26°C to form.
- They develop at latitudes usually greater than 5° from the equator due to the necessity of the Coriolis force.
- Regional terms include Hurricane (North Atlantic/Pacific), Typhoon (Western North Pacific), and Willy-willy (Eastern part of the Southern Indian Ocean).

#### Section Excerpt

Always form over oceans where sea surface temperature is greater than 26°C. Develop at latitudes usually greater than 5° from equator in the presence of Coriolis force. Terms for Tropical Cyclones: Hurricane – North Atlantic, Eastern North Pacific and South Pacific Ocean. Cyclone – Indian Ocean. Typhoon – Western North Pacific Ocean. Willy-willy: Eastern part of the Southern Indian Ocean.

#### Claims

- Tropical cyclones require a sea surface temperature greater than 26°C to form.
- Tropical cyclones develop at latitudes usually greater than 5° from the equator due to the necessity of the Coriolis force.
- Tropical cyclones are known by different regional names, such as Hurricanes in the North Atlantic, Typhoons in the Western North Pacific, and Willy-willies in the Eastern part of the Southern Indian Ocean.

### Disaster-Related Reports and Indices

- Pages: 102
- Focus: Key indices including the Global Drought Outlook, Disaster Risk Index (DRI), and District Flood Severity Index.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- The Global Drought Outlook, 2025 is released by the OECD.
- The Disaster Risk Index (DRI) was formally adopted by the 15th Finance Commission to guide disaster funding and distribute NDRF funds.
- The DRI composite score is based on the probability of hazards (70) and vulnerability (30).
- The District Flood Severity Index was developed by IIT Delhi and Gandhinagar researchers to quantify flood severity using occurrence and damage variables.

#### Section Excerpt

Global Drought Outlook, 2025 Released by: Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD). Disaster Risk Index (DRI)... Genesis: 15th Finance Commission (2021–26) formally adopted it to guide disaster funding. It integrated state’s DRI score into a formula for distributing NDRF and state contingency funds. Components: DRI uses probability of hazards (score of 70) and vulnerability (score of 30) to arrive at a composite score. District Flood Severity Index Developed by: Researchers from IIT Delhi and Gandhinagar... Consists of six factors classified in two groups: Variables representing occurrence of floods... Variables representing damage due to floods.

#### Claims

- The Global Drought Outlook, 2025 is released by the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD).
- The Disaster Risk Index (DRI) was formally adopted by the 15th Finance Commission to guide disaster funding and distribute National Disaster Response Fund (NDRF) allocations.
- The composite score of the Disaster Risk Index (DRI) is calculated using the probability of hazards, which carries a weightage of 70, and vulnerability, which carries a weightage of 30.
- The District Flood Severity Index, developed by researchers from IIT Delhi and Gandhinagar, quantifies flood severity using variables representing the occurrence of floods and the damage caused by them.

## UNESCO Geoparks and Seabed Mining

- Pages: 103-104

### Polymetallic Sulphides & International Seabed Authority (ISA)

- Pages: 103-104
- Focus: India's deep-sea exploration contracts, characteristics of polymetallic sulphides/nodules, and the mandate/initiatives of the ISA.
- Question quota hint: 4
- Claim count: 6

#### Evidence Bullets

- India signed a 15-year contract with the ISA for exploring polymetallic sulphides in the Carlsberg Ridge, located in the Arabian Sea.
- India holds other exploration contracts for Polymetallic Nodules in the Central Indian Ocean Basin and PMS in the Indian Ocean Ridge.
- India's exploration approval for the Afanasy-Nikitin Sea (ANS) mount is pending, as the territory is claimed by Sri Lanka.
- Polymetallic sulphides are rich in copper, zinc, gold, and silver, and form where hot, mineral-rich fluids from the Earth's mantle enter the ocean.
- The International Seabed Authority (ISA) is an autonomous organization established in 1994 under UNCLOS, headquartered in Kingston, Jamaica.
- ISA initiatives include the Deep-Sea Biobank Initiative (DBI) 2025, AREA2030, and the Sustainable Seabed Knowledge Initiative (SSKI).

#### Section Excerpt

India signed a 15-year exploration contract for polymetallic sulphides (PMS) with International Seabed Authority (ISA) in Carlsberg Ridge. This is the first licence granted globally for exploring polymetallic sulphur nodules in the Carlsberg Ridge... Other Indian Contracts: Polymetallic Nodules in the Central Indian Ocean Basin and PMS in the Indian Ocean Ridge. Yet to be approved: Afanasy-Nikitin Sea (ANS) mount... claimed by Sri Lanka. Polymetallic sulphides are rich sources of metals such as copper, zinc, gold, and silver... ISA Location: Kingston, Jamaica. Established in 1994 under UNCLOS. Initiatives: Deep-Sea Biobank Initiative (DBI) 2025, AREA2030, Sustainable Seabed Knowledge Initiative (SSKI).

#### Claims

- India signed a 15-year exploration contract with the International Seabed Authority (ISA) for exploring polymetallic sulphides in the Carlsberg Ridge.
- India holds an exploration contract for Polymetallic Nodules specifically in the Central Indian Ocean Basin.
- India's exploration approval for the Afanasy-Nikitin Sea (ANS) mount is pending because the territory is claimed by Sri Lanka.
- Polymetallic sulphides are rich in copper, zinc, gold, and silver, and are formed where hot, mineral-rich fluids from the Earth's mantle enter the ocean.
- The International Seabed Authority (ISA) is an autonomous organization established in 1994 under UNCLOS, with its headquarters in Kingston, Jamaica.
- The Deep-Sea Biobank Initiative (DBI) 2025, AREA2030, and the Sustainable Seabed Knowledge Initiative (SSKI) are initiatives launched by the International Seabed Authority (ISA).

### Global Geoparks Network (GGN) & UNESCO Global Geoparks

- Pages: 103
- Focus: UNESCO Global Geoparks framework, GGN membership criteria, and India's current status.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- GGN is a non-profit International Association under UNESCO that establishes ethical standards for Global Geoparks.
- UNESCO Global Geoparks (UGGP) were introduced in 2015 under the International Geosciences and Geoparks Programme (IGGP).
- UGGP status is not permanent and must be reassessed every four years.
- Membership in the Global Geoparks Network (GGN) is obligatory for all UGGPs.
- There are currently 229 UNESCO Global Geoparks globally, but none are located in India.

#### Section Excerpt

GGN is a non-profit International Association founded under UNESCO, which establishes ethical standards to be adopted by Global Geoparks. Introduced in 2015 as a key component of the International Geosciences and Geoparks Programme (IGGP). Geoparks: Single, unified geographical areas where landscapes of international geological significance are managed with a holistic concept... UGGP status is not permanent; it is reassessed every four years. Mandatory Networking: Membership of the GGN is obligatory for UGGPs. Current Status: 229 UNESCO Global Geoparks in 50 countries (none in India).

#### Claims

- The Global Geoparks Network (GGN) is a non-profit International Association founded under UNESCO that establishes ethical standards for Global Geoparks.
- UNESCO Global Geoparks (UGGP) were introduced in 2015 as a component of the International Geosciences and Geoparks Programme (IGGP).
- The UNESCO Global Geopark (UGGP) status is not permanent and is subject to reassessment every four years.
- Membership in the Global Geoparks Network (GGN) is mandatory for all UNESCO Global Geoparks.
- Currently, there are no UNESCO Global Geoparks located in India.

### Bharat Forecast System (BFS) & Mission Mausam

- Pages: 104
- Focus: India's indigenous high-resolution weather forecast system, its technical features, and related meteorological initiatives.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Bharat Forecast System (BFS) is the world's first indigenously developed high-resolution weather forecast system, created by IITM, Pune.
- BFS improves India's weather prediction resolution from 12 km to 6 km, which is ahead of global models that operate at 9-14 km.
- The system integrates real-time data from 40 Doppler Weather Radars, which use the Doppler effect to gather velocity data from particles.
- BFS is powered by High-Performance Computing (HPC) systems named Arka (IITM Pune) and Arunika (NCMRWF, Delhi).
- Mission Mausam was launched in 2024 by the Ministry of Earth Sciences to improve weather and climate services.

#### Section Excerpt

Ministry of Earth Sciences unveiled BFS, world's first indigenously developed high-resolution weather forecast systems. Developed by: Indian Institute of Tropical Meteorology (IITM), Pune... Enhances India's weather prediction resolution from 12 km to 6 km... Integrates real-time inputs from 40 Doppler Weather Radar. Positions India ahead of countries like US, UK, and EU by achieving 6 km resolution. Powered by High-Performance Computing (HPC) systems - Arka (IITM Pune) and Arunika (National Centre for Medium Range Weather Forecasting, Delhi). Mission Mausam: Launched in 2024 by Ministry of Earth Sciences (MoES).

#### Claims

- Bharat Forecast System (BFS) is an indigenously developed high-resolution weather forecast system created by the Indian Institute of Tropical Meteorology (IITM), Pune.
- The Bharat Forecast System (BFS) enhances India's weather prediction resolution to 6 km, positioning it ahead of models from the US, UK, and EU.
- The Bharat Forecast System (BFS) integrates real-time data from 40 Doppler Weather Radars.
- Arka and Arunika are High-Performance Computing (HPC) systems that power the Bharat Forecast System (BFS).
- Mission Mausam was launched in 2024 by the Ministry of Earth Sciences (MoES) to improve weather and climate services.

## Rainfall LPA and AMOC

- Topic: Geography
- Pages: 105-107
- Rationale: Explains the Long-Period Average (LPA) for monsoon, reverse faulting, and the significance of the AMOC slowdown.

### Pacific Ring of Fire and Reverse Faulting

- Pages: 105-106
- Focus: Geological characteristics of the Pacific Ring of Fire, plate boundaries, and the mechanics of reverse faulting.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Reverse faulting (thrust faulting) is caused by compressional forces pushing one block of Earth's crust over another.
- The Pacific Ring of Fire accounts for approximately 75% of the world's active volcanoes and 90% of its earthquakes.
- Convergent boundaries in the Ring of Fire create subduction zones, leading to volcanism and deep ocean trenches like the Mariana Trench.
- Divergent boundaries, such as the East Pacific Rise, create seafloor spreading and rift valleys featuring hydrothermal vents.

#### Section Excerpt

A magnitude 8.8 earthquake struck Russia’s Kamchatka Peninsula... potentially due to shallow reverse faulting... Reverse faulting (or thrust faulting) occurs when a block of Earth's crust is pushed up over another due to compressional forces... Pacific Ring of Fire: Also called Circum-Pacific Belt, it is a horseshoe-shaped belt around the rim of the Pacific Ocean... Accounts for ~75% of the world’s active volcanoes and ~90% of the world’s earthquakes.

#### Claims

- Reverse faulting, or thrust faulting, occurs when compressional forces push one block of the Earth's crust over another.
- The Pacific Ring of Fire accounts for approximately 75 percent of the world's active volcanoes and 90 percent of its earthquakes.
- Convergent boundaries in the Pacific Ring of Fire create subduction zones that lead to volcanism and the formation of deep ocean trenches.
- Divergent boundaries like the East Pacific Rise create seafloor spreading and rift valleys that feature hydrothermal vents.

### Long-Period Average (LPA)

- Pages: 105
- Focus: Definition, calculation period, and IMD's rainfall categorization based on LPA.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- LPA is calculated over a long period, usually 30-50 years, with the IMD currently using rainfall data from 1971 to 2020.
- Normal rainfall is categorized as 96% to 104% of the LPA.
- Deficient rainfall, indicating drought-like conditions, is defined as less than 90% of the LPA.
- Above Normal rainfall is 105% to 110% of the LPA.

#### Section Excerpt

The India Meteorological Department (IMD) has forecast ‘above normal’ rainfall — 105% of the long-period average (LPA) of 87 cm (1971-2020)... Concept: It refers to the average rainfall recorded over a specific region during a defined time interval. Period: It is calculated over a long period, usually 30-50 years... Deficient: < 90% | Meaning: Drought-like conditions... Normal: 96% – 104% | Meaning: Ideal, expected rainfall.

#### Claims

- The Long-Period Average (LPA) for rainfall is calculated over a period of 30 to 50 years.
- The India Meteorological Department (IMD) currently uses rainfall data from the period 1971 to 2020 to calculate the Long-Period Average (LPA).
- According to the IMD, 'Normal' rainfall is categorized as 96% to 104% of the Long-Period Average (LPA).
- According to the IMD, 'Deficient' rainfall is defined as less than 90% of the Long-Period Average (LPA) and indicates drought-like conditions.
- According to the IMD, 'Above Normal' rainfall is categorized as 105% to 110% of the Long-Period Average (LPA).

### True Polar Wander (TPW)

- Pages: 105
- Focus: Concept of planetary reorientation, its drivers, and effects on Earth's rotation and day length.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- True Polar Wander (TPW) involves the rotation of the solid Earth (crust and mantle) about the liquid outer core to maintain rotational balance.
- Natural drivers of TPW include glacial melting, tectonic plate shifts, and ocean swell, while human activities like dam construction also contribute.
- Shifting poles move mass from the poles to the equator, making the Earth slightly more flattened and slowing its spin, which results in longer days.

#### Section Excerpt

A recent study revealed that dam construction has shifted Earth’s rotational axis by over 1 meter since 1835 i.e., they have driven True Polar Wander (TPW). About True Polar Wander (TPW) or planetary reorientation: Rotation of the solid Earth (crust and mantle) about the liquid outer core... Effects of Shifting Poles: Longer Days as melting ice moves mass from the poles to the equator, making Earth slightly more flattened. This slows down its spin, causing longer days.

#### Claims

- True Polar Wander (TPW) refers to the rotation of the solid Earth, comprising the crust and mantle, about the liquid outer core.
- Human activities, such as large-scale dam construction, can drive True Polar Wander by shifting the Earth's rotational axis.
- The movement of mass from the poles to the equator due to melting ice flattens the Earth slightly, which slows down its spin and leads to longer days.

### Atlantic Meridional Overturning Circulation (AMOC)

- Pages: 106-107
- Focus: Mechanism, significance, and potential impacts of the weakening of the AMOC.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- AMOC is driven by differences in water temperature and salinity, circulating warm water north and cold water south.
- Warm tropical water moves towards the poles, cools, becomes dense, and sinks in the North Atlantic before flowing south.
- AMOC influences global climate patterns, including the Indian monsoon, and moderates Europe's climate by transporting heat from the tropics.
- A slowdown in AMOC could lead to colder temperatures in Europe, reduced ocean carbon uptake, and sea-level rise across the U.S. East Coast.

#### Section Excerpt

AMOC: A system of ocean currents that circulates water within the Atlantic Ocean, bringing warm water north and cold water south. Driving Force: Differences in water temperature and salinity... Significance of AMOC: Influences rainfall patterns, including Indian monsoon. Heat Transport from the tropics to higher latitudes, moderating Europe’s climate... Potential Impacts of AMOC Slowdown: AMOC carbon feedback: Reduction of ocean carbon uptake... Colder temperatures in Europe...

#### Claims

- The Atlantic Meridional Overturning Circulation (AMOC) is driven by differences in water temperature and salinity.
- During the AMOC process, warm tropical water moves towards the poles, cools, becomes denser, and sinks in the North Atlantic before flowing south.
- AMOC moderates Europe's climate by transporting heat from the tropics to higher latitudes.
- The AMOC influences global climate patterns, including the Indian monsoon.
- A slowdown in the AMOC could lead to colder temperatures in Europe, reduced ocean carbon uptake, and sea-level rise across the U.S. East Coast.

### Delamination and Indian Plate Movement

- Pages: 107
- Focus: The new theory of delamination explaining the splitting of the Indian Continental Plate.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Delamination is a process where the dense lower section of a tectonic plate peels away and sinks into the Earth's mantle.
- The Indian Continental Plate is bordered by four major plates: the Eurasian, Arabian, African, and Australian Plates.
- Traditional theories for the Indian-Eurasian plate convergence are underplating (lower crust sliding beneath) and subduction (one plate sliding beneath another).

#### Section Excerpt

New research suggests that Indian Continental Plate is splitting apart and proposes a new theory explaining movement of the Indian Plate called ‘Delamination’. About Delamination: It is where the Indian plate's dense lower section peels away and sinks into Earth's mantle as it slides beneath the Eurasian plate... Two traditional theories explain this: Underplating: The denser Indian lower crust slides beneath the Eurasian crust. Subduction: One plate slides beneath another.

#### Claims

- Delamination is a tectonic process where the dense lower section of a plate peels away and sinks into the Earth's mantle.
- The Indian Continental Plate is bordered by the Eurasian, Arabian, African, and Australian Plates.
- In the context of the Indian-Eurasian plate convergence, underplating involves the denser lower crust sliding beneath the Eurasian crust, whereas subduction involves an entire plate sliding beneath another.

### Miscellaneous Geography Terms: Solar Tornado, Cold Pools, and Deep Seafloor

- Pages: 107
- Focus: Definitions and characteristics of specific geographical and astronomical phenomena in the news.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Solar tornadoes (tornado prominences) are made of ionized gas (plasma) held by magnetic fields and can reach temperatures around 250,000 °C.
- Cold pools form when evaporating rain cools the air, making it heavier, causing it to sink and spread across the ground like a shallow bubble.
- The Deep Ocean is typically defined as the sea and seabed below 200 meters, where light rapidly decreases and the Twilight Zone begins.

#### Section Excerpt

Term/Concept: Solar Tornado... made of ionized gas (plasma), held in place by magnetic fields... Term/Concept: Cold Pools... Small-scale areas of evaporatively cooled downdraft air that spread on the surface underneath precipitating clouds... Term/Concept: Earth’s Deep Seafloor... seabed below the depth at which light starts to decrease rapidly, typically around 200 meters...

#### Claims

- Solar tornadoes are composed of ionized gas or plasma and are held in place by magnetic fields.
- Cold pools are formed when evaporating rain cools the air, causing it to become heavier, sink, and spread across the surface as a downdraft beneath precipitating clouds.
- The Deep Ocean is typically defined as the sea and seabed below a depth of 200 meters, which marks the beginning of the Twilight Zone where light rapidly decreases.

## Deep Ocean Zones and NCPOR

- Topic: Geography
- Pages: 108-109
- Rationale: Covers the mesopelagic zone, polar anticyclones, and the role of the National Centre for Polar and Ocean Research.

### Arabian Sea Mini Warm Pool

- Pages: 108
- Focus: Definition, location, duration, and impact on the Indian Summer Monsoon.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Located in the southeastern Arabian Sea near the Kerala coast with SST exceeding 28.5 degrees Celsius.
- Forms annually during April and May just before the Indian Summer Monsoon.
- Acts as a self-correcting mechanism helping the monsoon recover from previous El Nino disruptions.

#### Section Excerpt

The Arabian Sea Mini Warm Pool (MWP) is a patch of unusually warm sea surface temperatures (exceeding 28.5 degrees Celsius) in the southeastern Arabian Sea near the Kerala coast. It forms annually during April and May before the Indian Summer Monsoon and acts as a self-correcting mechanism to help the monsoon recover from previous El Nino disruptions.

#### Claims

- The Arabian Sea Mini Warm Pool is located in the southeastern Arabian Sea near the Kerala coast, characterized by sea surface temperatures exceeding 28.5 degrees Celsius.
- The Arabian Sea Mini Warm Pool forms annually during April and May, just before the onset of the Indian Summer Monsoon.
- The Arabian Sea Mini Warm Pool functions as a self-correcting mechanism that assists the Indian Summer Monsoon in recovering from prior El Nino disruptions.

### Deep Ocean Characteristics and Exploration

- Pages: 108
- Focus: Physical conditions, biodiversity in the Mesopelagic Zone, and the significance of deep ocean exploration.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Average temperature is 4 degrees Celsius with pressure 40 to 110 times Earth's atmosphere.
- Mesopelagic Zone (200m-1000m) holds about 90 percent of world's fish by weight.
- Exploration yields energy sources like methane hydrate, polymetallic nodules, and new drugs.

#### Section Excerpt

Deep ocean conditions include an average temperature of 4 degrees Celsius and extreme pressure. The Mesopelagic Zone (200m-1000m) contains about 90 percent of the world's fish by weight. Exploration is significant for energy sources, new drugs, polymetallic nodules, and climate change mitigation.

#### Claims

- The deep ocean is characterized by an average temperature of 4 degrees Celsius and extreme pressure ranging from 40 to 110 times the Earth's atmospheric pressure.
- The Mesopelagic Zone, situated between 200m and 1000m depth, holds about 90 percent of the world's fish by weight.
- Deep ocean exploration yields significant resources including energy sources like methane hydrate, polymetallic nodules, and compounds for new drugs.

### Mercator's Map Projection

- Pages: 108
- Focus: Characteristics, distortions, and recent campaigns against the Mercator projection.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Conformal map designed in 1569 that preserves local shapes and angles.
- Distorts scale by enlarging landmasses near the poles and shrinking equatorial regions.
- African Union endorsed the Correct the Map campaign to replace it with the Equal Earth map.

#### Section Excerpt

Designed in 1569 by Gerardus Mercator, this conformal map preserves local shapes and angles but distorts scale, making polar landmasses appear larger and equatorial regions smaller. For example, Africa appears roughly the size of Greenland despite being 14 times larger. The African Union endorsed the Correct the Map campaign to replace it with alternatives like the Equal Earth map.

#### Claims

- The Mercator map projection is a conformal map that preserves local shapes and angles.
- The Mercator projection distorts scale by enlarging landmasses near the poles and shrinking equatorial regions.
- The African Union endorsed the Correct the Map campaign to replace the Mercator projection with the Equal Earth map.

### Polar Anticyclone

- Pages: 108
- Focus: Formation mechanism and air circulation patterns of polar anticyclones.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Created by intense cooling of surface air causing dense air to sink.
- High-pressure area surrounded by low-pressure zones with outward flowing winds.
- Circulation is clockwise in the Northern Hemisphere and anti-clockwise in the Southern Hemisphere.

#### Section Excerpt

Polar anticyclones are high-pressure wind systems created by intense cooling of surface air layers. Surface cooling causes dense air to sink, which is replaced by high-altitude air, building high pressure. Winds flow outward from the center, circulating clockwise in the Northern Hemisphere and anti-clockwise in the Southern Hemisphere.

#### Claims

- Polar anticyclones are high-pressure wind systems formed by the intense cooling of surface air, which causes dense air to sink.
- Winds in a polar anticyclone flow outward from the high-pressure center.
- The wind circulation in polar anticyclones is clockwise in the Northern Hemisphere and anti-clockwise in the Southern Hemisphere.

### Thirstwave

- Pages: 108
- Focus: Definition, criteria, and factors driving extreme atmospheric thirst.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Defined by high dryness and aggressive atmospheric demand for moisture.
- Requires at least 3 consecutive days of evaporative demand greater than the historical 90th percentile.
- Driven by temperature, wind speed, humidity, and sunshine.

#### Section Excerpt

A thirstwave involves periods of extreme atmospheric thirst that rapidly dry out the landscape, defined by high dryness and aggressive moisture demand. It occurs when daily evaporative demand exceeds its historical 90th percentile for at least 3 consecutive days. Factors driving this include temperature, wind speed, humidity, and sunshine.

#### Claims

- A thirstwave is a period of extreme atmospheric thirst characterized by high dryness and aggressive moisture demand that rapidly dries out the landscape.
- A thirstwave occurs when daily evaporative demand exceeds its historical 90th percentile for at least 3 consecutive days.
- The factors driving a thirstwave include temperature, wind speed, humidity, and sunshine.

### National Centre of Polar and Ocean Research (NCPOR)

- Pages: 109
- Focus: Genesis, governing body, key roles, and newly launched facilities of NCPOR.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Autonomous institution of the Ministry of Earth Sciences established in 1998.
- Maintains research stations: Maitri and Bharati (Antarctica), Himadri (Arctic), and Himansh (Himalayas).
- Leads the Deep Ocean Mission and implements India's Arctic Policy and Antarctica Act.
- Recently launched Polar Bhavan (laboratories/museum) and Sagar Bhavan (ice core laboratories).

#### Section Excerpt

NCPOR is an autonomous institution under the Ministry of Earth Sciences, established in 1998. It maintains India's research stations in Antarctica (Maitri, Bharati), the Arctic (Himadri), and the Himalayas (Himansh). It leads the Deep Ocean Mission and aids in implementing India's Arctic Policy and Antarctica Act. Recent facilities include Polar Bhavan and Sagar Bhavan.

#### Claims

- The National Centre of Polar and Ocean Research (NCPOR) is an autonomous institution established in 1998 under the Ministry of Earth Sciences.
- NCPOR maintains India's research stations in Antarctica, which include Maitri and Bharati.
- NCPOR is responsible for maintaining the Himadri research station in the Arctic and the Himansh research station in the Himalayas.
- NCPOR is the lead agency for the Deep Ocean Mission and aids in the implementation of India's Arctic Policy and Antarctica Act.
- NCPOR recently launched Polar Bhavan, which houses laboratories and a museum, and Sagar Bhavan, which contains ice core laboratories.

- Barren Island in the Andaman Sea is India's only active volcano.

- Barren Island, situated in the Andaman Sea, is India's only active volcano.
- The Andaman Sea falls under Seismic Zone V, is part of the Coral Triangle, and is bounded by Myanmar, Thailand, Malaysia, and Indonesia.
- Kariyachalli Island is located in the Gulf of Mannar.

- Beas River originates at Beas Kund (Rohtang Pass) and joins the Sutlej at Harike, Punjab.

- Subansiri River, known as the Gold River, is the largest tributary of the Brahmaputra.
- Mandovi/Mahadayi River originates in Bhimgad (Western Ghats), flows through Goa, Karnataka, and Maharashtra, and features the Dudhsagar waterfall.
- Subarnarekha River flows through Jharkhand, Odisha, and West Bengal, and hosts the Hundru Falls.

Details major rivers in the news: Beas (Ravi and Beas Waters Tribunal, joins Sutlej), Chenab (Sawalkot HEP, formed by Chandra and Bhaga), Subansiri (Lower Hydroelectric Project, largest Brahmaputra tributary), Kopili (NW-57, Meghalaya/Assam), Siyom (Arunachal Pradesh HEPs), Mandovi/Mahadayi (water tribunal, Dudhsagar falls), and Subarnarekha (flash floods, NW-96, Hundru Falls).

#### Claims

- The Beas River originates at Beas Kund near Rohtang Pass and joins the Sutlej River at Harike in Punjab.
- The Chenab River is formed by the confluence of the Chandra and Bhaga rivers and is the largest tributary of the Indus River.
- The Subansiri River, also known as the Gold River, is the largest tributary of the Brahmaputra River.

- The Subarnarekha River flows through Jharkhand, Odisha, and West Bengal, and hosts the Hundru Falls.
- The Kopili River flows through Meghalaya and Assam and is designated as National Waterway 57 (NW-57).

Denmark: India and Denmark reaffirm Green Strategic Partnership... Ethiopia: UN Food Systems Summit +4 Stocktake held in Addis Ababa... Tuvalu: Signed the 2023 Falepili Union Treaty with Australia... Ecuador: Indigenous groups criticize oil drilling expansion in the Amazon.

#### Claims

- Vanuatu approached the International Court of Justice to classify environmental destruction as ecocide.
- The Second WHO Global Conference on Air Pollution and Health was held in Cartagena, Colombia.
- India and Denmark share a Green Strategic Partnership.
- Ethiopia hosted the UN Food Systems Summit +4 Stocktake in Addis Ababa.
- Tuvalu signed the 2023 Falepili Union Treaty with Australia to address threats from rising sea levels.
- In Ecuador, indigenous groups have criticized the expansion of oil drilling in the Amazon.

### Kaziranga National Park and Tiger Reserve (Assam)

- Pages: 118
- Focus: Ecological features, fauna, river systems, and recent census techniques at Kaziranga.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 8

#### Evidence Bullets

- First-ever grassland bird census was conducted using Acoustic Monitoring Technique.
- Located on the Brahmaputra floodplain, at the foothills of Karbi-Anglong.
- Diffalu and Moradifalu rivers flow through the park.
- Hosts 70% of the One-Horned Rhino population.
- Records the 3rd highest tiger density in India after Bandipur and Corbett.
- Recognized as an Important Bird Area by BirdLife International.

#### Section Excerpt

First-ever grassland bird census was held here using Acoustic Monitoring Technique. Location: Brahmaputra floodplain, at foothills of Karbi-Anglong. River: Diffalu and Moradifalu. Forest type: Alluvial grasslands, semi-evergreen and moist deciduous forests, wetlands, and sandy chaurs. Key Fauna: One-Horned Rhino (70% of population), Tiger, Eastern swamp deer, Elephant, Hoolock gibbon, Capped langur and Gangetic River Dolphin etc. Recorded 3rd highest tiger density in India after Karnataka's Bandipur and Uttarakhand's Corbett National Park. Recognized as an Important Bird Area by BirdLife International.

#### Claims

- The first-ever grassland bird census in Kaziranga National Park was conducted using the Acoustic Monitoring Technique.
- Kaziranga National Park is located on the Brahmaputra floodplain at the foothills of Karbi-Anglong.
- The Diffalu and Moradifalu rivers flow through Kaziranga National Park.
- The vegetation of Kaziranga National Park includes alluvial grasslands, semi-evergreen forests, and moist deciduous forests.
- Kaziranga National Park hosts 70% of the One-Horned Rhino population.
- Kaziranga National Park records the 3rd highest tiger density in India, after Bandipur and Corbett National Parks.
- The fauna of Kaziranga National Park includes the Eastern swamp deer, Hoolock gibbon, Capped langur, and Gangetic River Dolphin.
- Kaziranga National Park is recognized as an Important Bird Area by BirdLife International.

### Tsarap Chu Conservation Reserve (Himachal Pradesh)

- Question quota hint: 2
