- Fauna includes snow leopard, Tibetan wolf, bharal (blue sheep), Himalayan ibex, kiang (wild ass), and Tibetan argali.

#### Section Excerpt

Himachal Pradesh notified it (India's largest conservation reserve) in Spiti Valley. Location: Confluence of Unam River and Charap Nala. Bounded by UT of Ladakh to north, the Kibber Wildlife Sanctuary extending up to Malang Nala and Lungar Lungpa to east, Kabjima Nala to south and Chandratal Wildlife Sanctuary to west. Fauna: Known for snow leopard, Tibetan wolf, bharal (blue sheep), Himalayan ibex, kiang (wild ass), and Tibetan argali, rare bird species such as Rose Finch, Tibetan Raven, etc.

#### Claims

- Tsarap Chu Conservation Reserve is India's largest conservation reserve, located in the Spiti Valley of Himachal Pradesh.
- Tsarap Chu Conservation Reserve is situated at the confluence of the Unam River and Charap Nala.
- Tsarap Chu Conservation Reserve is bounded by the UT of Ladakh to the north, Kibber Wildlife Sanctuary to the east, and Chandratal Wildlife Sanctuary to the west.
- The fauna of Tsarap Chu Conservation Reserve includes the snow leopard, Tibetan wolf, bharal (blue sheep), Himalayan ibex, kiang (wild ass), and Tibetan argali.

- Characterized by Phumdis, which are floating islands of vegetation.

#### Section Excerpt

Manipur Keibul Lamjao National Park - Context: Study links land use to water pollution in Manipur's Loktak Lake. Location: Bishnupur and Thoubal district of Manipur. Only floating park in the world. Largest area of Phumdi (floating Islands of vegetation) in Loktak lake is in this park. Loktak lake, a Ramsar site and Montreux Record site... Fauna: Brow-antlered deer (Sangai).

#### Claims

- Keibul Lamjao National Park is the only floating national park in the world.
- Loktak Lake, where Keibul Lamjao National Park is located, is recognized as both a Ramsar site and a Montreux Record site.
- Phumdis are floating islands of vegetation characteristic of Loktak Lake and Keibul Lamjao National Park.
- Keibul Lamjao National Park is the primary habitat for the Sangai, also known as the Brow-antlered deer.

### Bhagirathi Eco Sensitive Zone

- Pages: 120
- Focus: Ecological significance, regulatory framework, and location of the Bhagirathi ESZ.
- Question quota hint: 1
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Created to protect the pristine stretch of the River Ganga between Gaumukh and Uttarkashi.
- Notified by MoEF&CC under the Environment (Protection) Act, 1986.
- Eco-sensitive Zones act as 'Shock Absorbers' around Protected Areas and wildlife corridors.
- Requires a Zonal Master Plan (ZMP) based on a watershed approach.

#### Section Excerpt

Uttarakhand Bhagirathi Eco Sensitive Zone (ESZ) - Context: Recently, Uttarakhand Government granted approval for Netala bypass project in fragile Bhagirathi ESZ despite previous rejections... Created to protect River Ganga's most pristine stretch between Gaumukh and Uttarkashi town. Eco-sensitive Zones are ecologically fragile areas around Protected Areas... Notification: By the Ministry of Environment, Forest and Climate Change (MoEF&CC) in 2012... under Environment (Protection) Act, 1986.

#### Claims

- The Bhagirathi Eco Sensitive Zone was established to protect the stretch of the River Ganga between Gaumukh and Uttarkashi.
- Eco-sensitive Zones are notified by the Ministry of Environment, Forest and Climate Change under the Environment (Protection) Act, 1986.
- Eco-sensitive Zones act as 'shock absorbers' around Protected Areas and wildlife corridors.
- The management of the Bhagirathi Eco Sensitive Zone requires a Zonal Master Plan based on a watershed approach.

### Salkhan Fossil Park

- Pages: 120
- Focus: Geo-heritage significance, stromatolites, and Great Oxidation Event connection of Salkhan Fossil Park.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Added to the UNESCO Tentative List for World Heritage Sites.
- Located in the Kaimur Range, part of the Vindhya range in Uttar Pradesh.
- Features approximately 1.4 billion-year-old Stromatolite fossils created by cyanobacteria.
- The fossilized microbial structures record the Great Oxidation Event.

#### Section Excerpt

Salkhan Fossil Park - Context: Salkhan Fossil Park added to UNESCO Tentative List For World Heritage Sites, officially known as Sonbhadra Fossils Park, Sonbhadra, Uttar Pradesh... Location: Kaimur Range (part of Vindhya range), adjacent to Kaimur Wildlife Sanctuary. One of oldest and most well-preserved sites in world (fossils dating ~1.4 billion years). Site's fossil assemblage features Stromatolites created by communities of cyanobacteria... record Great Oxidation Event.

#### Claims

- Salkhan Fossil Park is located in the Kaimur Range, which is part of the Vindhya range in Uttar Pradesh.
- Salkhan Fossil Park features approximately 1.4 billion-year-old Stromatolite fossils created by communities of cyanobacteria.
- The fossilized microbial structures at Salkhan Fossil Park record the Great Oxidation Event.
- Salkhan Fossil Park has been added to the UNESCO Tentative List for World Heritage Sites.

### Sundarbans Tiger Reserve

- Pages: 121
- Focus: Expansion, geographical borders, and international designations of Sundarbans Tiger Reserve.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Now India's second-largest tiger reserve, behind Nagarjunasagar-Srisailam.
- The only mangrove forest in the world housing a significant tiger population.
- Bordered by the River Matla to the west and Rivers Bidya & Gomdi to the north-west.
- Holds designations as a UNESCO World Heritage Site, CA|TS, and MAB Programme site.

#### Section Excerpt

West Bengal. Sundarbans Tiger Reserve (STR). Context: STR is now India's second largest after expansion of its area was approved by National Board of Wildlife (NBWL). - Now STR is just behind Andhra Pradesh's Nagarjunasagar-Srisailam Tiger Reserve in size... Only mangrove forest (with Bangladesh) housing a significant tiger population. Borders: Bangladesh (east), Bay of Bengal (south), River Matla (west), Rivers Bidya & Gomdi (north-west). Associated Designations: UNESCO World Heritage Site, CA|TS (Conservation Assured | Tiger Standards), MAB.

#### Claims

- Sundarbans Tiger Reserve is India's second-largest tiger reserve, behind Nagarjunasagar-Srisailam Tiger Reserve.
- Sundarbans is the only mangrove forest in the world that houses a significant tiger population.
- Sundarbans Tiger Reserve is bordered by the River Matla to the west and Rivers Bidya and Gomdi to the north-west.
- Sundarbans Tiger Reserve holds multiple international designations including UNESCO World Heritage Site, CA|TS, and MAB Programme site.

## Snow Leopard, Rhino, and Nilgiri Tahr

- Topic: Species in News
- Pages: 122-123
- Rationale: Details the conservation status and habitats of high-altitude and montane species like the Snow Leopard and Nilgiri Tahr.

### Greater One-Horned Rhino (Indian Rhino)

- Pages: 122-123
- Focus: DNA profiling, habitat distribution, species comparison, and conservation initiatives of the Indian Rhino.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 6

#### Evidence Bullets

- IUCN Status of Indian Rhino is Vulnerable (VU); listed under WPA Schedule I and CITES Appendix I.
- Assam holds the world's largest population, with over 90% located in Kaziranga National Park.
- Indian Rhino is the largest of all Asian rhino species.
- Other rhino species statuses: White (Near Threatened), Black (Critically Endangered), Sumatran (Critically Endangered), Javan (Critically Endangered).
- RhoDIS India is the DNA data library used for profiling rhino horns.

#### Section Excerpt

Assam Forest Department started DNA profiling of Rhino horns and add it to Rhino DNA Index System (RhoDIS) India DNA data library. Conservation Status: WPA, 1972: Schedule I; CITES: Appendix I; IUCN Status: VU (Vulnerable). Habitat: Assam has the world's largest population. More than 90% of them are in Kaziranga National Park. Characteristics: One among 5 species of rhino: 2 African: White Rhino (Near Threatened), Black Rhino (Critically Endangered). 3 Asian: Sumatran (Critically Endangered), Javan (Critically Endangered), and Indian Rhino. Indian Rhino is the largest of all Asian rhino species. Usually solitary. Conservation initiatives: National Rhino Conservation Strategy 2019; New Delhi Declaration on Asian Rhinos 2019; Indian Rhino Vision 2020.

#### Claims

- The IUCN status of the Greater One-Horned Rhino (Indian Rhino) is Vulnerable.
- Assam holds the world's largest population of the Greater One-Horned Rhino, with over 90% located in Kaziranga National Park.
- The Indian Rhino is the largest of all Asian rhino species.
- The Sumatran and Javan rhinos are both listed as Critically Endangered.
- Among African rhinos, the White Rhino is Near Threatened while the Black Rhino is Critically Endangered.
- RhoDIS India is a DNA data library used for profiling rhino horns.

### Snow Leopard

- Pages: 122
- Focus: Habitat, characteristics, conservation status, and international/national conservation efforts for the Snow Leopard.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 6

#### Evidence Bullets

- IUCN Status is Vulnerable (VU); listed under WPA Schedule I, CITES Appendix I, and CMS Appendix I.
- Found in mountainous regions of J&K, Ladakh, HP, Uttarakhand, Sikkim, and Arunachal Pradesh.
- Hemis National Park, Kargil, and Leh have the highest extensive densities globally.
- Unlike other big cats, snow leopards cannot roar.
- Conservation initiatives include the Bishkek Declaration (2017), Samarkand Resolution (2024), and the CaTRAT (Camera Trap data Repository and Analysis Tool).

#### Section Excerpt

Study estimated 477 snow leopards in Ladakh. Habitat: Mountainous regions of South and Central Asia. India: Jammu & Kashmir, Ladakh, Himachal Pradesh, Uttarakhand, Sikkim and Arunachal Pradesh. Globally, Hemis National Park, Kargil, and Leh have highest extensive densities. Characteristics: Solitary animals; unlike other big cats they cannot roar. Conservation Status: WPA, 1972: Schedule I; CITES: Appendix I; CMS: Appendix I; IUCN Status: VU (Vulnerable). Conservation Efforts: Project Snow Leopard India; International Big Cat Alliance; Global Snow Leopard and Ecosystem Protection Programme; Bishkek Declaration (2017); Samarkand Resolution (2024); CaTRAT to identify Himalayan snow leopards.

#### Claims

- In India, snow leopards are found in the mountainous regions of Jammu & Kashmir, Ladakh, Himachal Pradesh, Uttarakhand, Sikkim, and Arunachal Pradesh.
- Hemis National Park, Kargil, and Leh have the highest extensive densities of snow leopards globally.
- Snow leopards are solitary animals and, unlike other big cats, they cannot roar.
- The snow leopard is listed as Vulnerable (VU) on the IUCN Red List, and is protected under WPA Schedule I, CITES Appendix I, and CMS Appendix I.
- The Bishkek Declaration (2017) and Samarkand Resolution (2024) are international initiatives focused on snow leopard conservation.
- CaTRAT (Camera Trap data Repository and Analysis Tool) is utilized to identify and track Himalayan snow leopards.

### Nilgiri Tahr

- Pages: 123
- Focus: Habitat, endemism, cultural significance, and conservation status of the Nilgiri Tahr.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 6

#### Evidence Bullets

- Endemic to the open montane grassland habitats of the Western Ghats.
- Eravikulam National Park in Kerala hosts the largest contiguous population.
- It is the only mountain ungulate in southern India.
- Mentioned in ancient Tamil literature such as Silappathikaram and Sivakasindamani.
- IUCN Status is Endangered (EN); it is the State animal of Tamil Nadu.

#### Section Excerpt

Traditional Nilgiri tahr habitats in Coimbatore Forest Division show signs of population revival. Habitat: Open montane grassland habitats. Endemic to Western Ghats. Eravikulam National Park, Kerala has the largest contiguous population. Characteristics: Only mountain ungulate in southern India. Locally known as Varaiaadu. Silappathikaram and Sivakasindamani mention its descriptions. Conservation Status: WPA, 1972: Schedule I; IUCN Status: Endangered (EN). Conservation Efforts: Project Nilgiri Tahr of Tamil Nadu. State animal of Tamil Nadu. Nilgiri Tahr Day (October 07).

#### Claims

- The Nilgiri Tahr is endemic to the open montane grassland habitats of the Western Ghats.
- Eravikulam National Park in Kerala hosts the largest contiguous population of the Nilgiri Tahr.
- The Nilgiri Tahr is the only mountain ungulate found in southern India.
- The Nilgiri Tahr is mentioned in ancient Tamil literature such as Silappathikaram and Sivakasindamani.
- The IUCN conservation status of the Nilgiri Tahr is Endangered (EN).
- The Nilgiri Tahr is the State animal of Tamil Nadu, which has launched Project Nilgiri Tahr.

### Alpine Musk Deer

- Pages: 124
- Focus: Habitat, unique physical traits, threats, and conservation status of the Alpine Musk Deer.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Native to India, Nepal, Bhutan, and China; inhabits alpine meadows and fir forests.
- Solitary, shy, herbivorous.
- Unique physical traits: possesses fangs, lacks antlers and gall bladder.
- Threatened by poaching for muskpods used in perfumes and traditional medicines.
- Conservation: WPA Schedule I, CITES Appendix I, IUCN Endangered.

#### Section Excerpt

Central Zoo Authority reported a mix-up in identifying Alpine musk deer for conservation breeding. Native to India, Nepal, Bhutan, and China, it inhabits alpine meadows and fir forests. It is solitary, shy, and herbivorous, uniquely possessing fangs but lacking antlers and a gall bladder. Threatened by poaching for muskpods. Conservation Status: WPA Schedule I, CITES Appendix I, IUCN Endangered.

#### Claims

- The Alpine Musk Deer is native to India, Nepal, Bhutan, and China, and primarily inhabits alpine meadows and fir forests.
- The Alpine Musk Deer uniquely possesses fangs but lacks antlers and a gall bladder.
- The Alpine Musk Deer is listed as Endangered on the IUCN Red List, and is protected under WPA Schedule I and CITES Appendix I.
- The Alpine Musk Deer is a solitary, shy, and herbivorous animal.
- The Alpine Musk Deer is highly threatened by poaching for its muskpods, which are utilized in perfumes and traditional medicines.

### Bonobo

- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Vocal communication shows compositionality, similar to human language.
- Endemic to the forests of the Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC).
- Share 98.7% of DNA with humans, making them our closest living relatives alongside chimpanzees.
- Peaceful species with female-led groups.
- Conservation: CITES Appendix I, IUCN Endangered.

#### Section Excerpt

A study found that vocal communication between Bonobos shows compositionality, similar to human language. Found only in the forests of the Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC). Like Chimpanzees, they share 98.7% of DNA with humans. They are peaceful, female-led, and smaller/darker than chimpanzees. Conservation Status: CITES Appendix I, IUCN Endangered.

#### Claims

- Bonobos are endemic exclusively to the forests of the Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC).
- Bonobos are characterized by a peaceful social structure with female-led groups.
- Bonobos share 98.7% of their DNA with humans, making them one of our closest living relatives alongside chimpanzees.
- The conservation status of the Bonobo is Endangered on the IUCN Red List and it is listed under CITES Appendix I.
- Vocal communication among Bonobos exhibits compositionality, a trait similar to human language.

### Greater Flamingo

- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Tamil Nadu notified the Greater Flamingo Sanctuary at Dhanushkodi.
- Breeds in shallow wetlands that are either saline or alkaline.
- Kachchh Desert Wildlife Sanctuary in Gujarat supports South Asia's only breeding ground of Greater Flamingos.
- Highly philopatric species (return to or remain near a particular site).
- IUCN Status is Least Concern (LC).

#### Section Excerpt

Greater Flamingo Context: Tamil Nadu notified Greater Flamingo Sanctuary at Dhanushkodi to preserve a critical stopover point along Central Asian Flyway. Habitat: Breeds in shallow wetlands that are either saline or alkaline... Kachchh Desert Wildlife Sanctuary in Great Rann of Kachchh (GRK) in Gujarat, is a unique Protected Area, supporting South Asia’s only breeding ground of Greater Flamingos... Characteristics: Great dispersal capacity outside breeding season, highly philopatric... Conservation Status: CITES: Appendix II. IUCN Status: LC (Least Concern).

#### Claims

- Tamil Nadu has notified the Greater Flamingo Sanctuary at Dhanushkodi to preserve a critical stopover point along the Central Asian Flyway.
- Greater Flamingos breed in shallow wetlands that are either saline or alkaline.
- The Kachchh Desert Wildlife Sanctuary in Gujarat supports South Asia's only breeding ground of Greater Flamingos.
- Greater Flamingos are highly philopatric, meaning they tend to return to or remain near a particular site.
- The Greater Flamingo is listed as Least Concern (LC) on the IUCN Red List and is included in CITES Appendix II.

Habitat: Warm, tropical waters of the Pacific, Atlantic, and Indian Oceans. Characteristics: Undergo unique mass nesting called arribadas. Smallest and most abundant of all sea turtles.

- Olive Ridley Turtles are the smallest and most abundant of all sea turtles.

## Insects, Lichens, and Tardigrades

### Clinidium lalitae

- Pages: 129
- Focus: Discovery, characteristics, and ecological role of the newly identified beetle species.
- Question quota hint: 1
- Claim count: 3

#### Evidence Bullets

- Identified by ZSI in Talle Valley Wildlife Sanctuary, Arunachal Pradesh.
- Belongs to subfamily Rhysodinae, a rare group of ground beetles.
- Plays a significant ecological role in nutrient cycling and soil health.

#### Section Excerpt

Scientists from the Zoological Survey of India (ZSI) identified a new species of beetle named Clinidium lalitae, in Talle Valley Wildlife Sanctuary, Arunachal Pradesh. It belongs to the subfamily Rhysodinae, a rare group of ground beetles inhibiting forest floors, and plays a significant ecological role in nutrient cycling and soil health.

#### Claims

- Clinidium lalitae is a newly identified species of beetle discovered in the Talle Valley Wildlife Sanctuary in Arunachal Pradesh.
- Clinidium lalitae belongs to the Rhysodinae subfamily, which is a rare group of ground beetles that inhabit forest floors.
- The Clinidium lalitae beetle contributes significantly to nutrient cycling and soil health in its ecosystem.

### Lichens

- Pages: 129
- Focus: Characteristics, distribution, ecological significance, and recent studies on Lichens.
- Question quota hint: 3
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Symbiotic association between fungus (mycobiont) and an alga or cyanobacterium (photobiont).
- Bioindicators of air pollution, especially SO2 and heavy metals.
- Pioneer species that act as first colonizers in ecological succession and aid in soil formation.
- India's first Lichen Park was established in 2020 in Munsiyari, Uttarakhand.
- Can survive and remain metabolically active under simulated Mars-like conditions.

#### Section Excerpt

Lichens can survive and remain metabolically active under simulated Mars-like conditions. They cover 8% of land surface, including extreme environments. India hosts over 2,700 species, with its first Lichen Park established in 2020 in Munsiyari, Uttarakhand. Lichens are a symbiotic association between a fungus (mycobiont) and an alga or cyanobacterium (photobiont). They act as bioindicators of air pollution (especially SO2) and are pioneer species in ecological succession, aiding in soil formation.

#### Claims

- Lichens are a symbiotic association between a fungus (mycobiont) and an alga or cyanobacterium (photobiont).
- Lichens act as bioindicators of air pollution, being particularly sensitive to sulfur dioxide (SO2) and heavy metals.
- Lichens are pioneer species that act as the first colonizers in ecological succession and aid in soil formation.
- India's first Lichen Park was established in 2020 in Munsiyari, Uttarakhand.
- Lichens are capable of surviving and remaining metabolically active under simulated Mars-like conditions.

### Cicadas

- Pages: 130
- Focus: Habitat, life cycle, and unique characteristics of Cicadas.
- Question quota hint: 1
- Claim count: 5

#### Evidence Bullets

- Returned to Kerala's Silent Valley National Park.
- Life cycle consists of three stages: egg, nymph, and adult.
- Produce exceptionally loud songs by the rapid buckling and unbuckling of drum-like tymbals.
- Adult females usually lay eggs in woody plant tissues.

#### Section Excerpt

Cicadas have returned to Kerala's Silent Valley National Park. They occur in warm and temperate biomes and have a life cycle of three stages: egg, nymph, and adult. Adult females usually lay eggs in woody plant tissues. Most species produce an exceptionally loud song by the rapid buckling and unbuckling of drum-like tymbals.

#### Claims

- Cicadas have recently returned to the Silent Valley National Park in Kerala.
- Cicadas are found in warm and temperate biomes.
- The life cycle of cicadas consists of three stages: egg, nymph, and adult.
- Adult female cicadas usually lay their eggs in woody plant tissues.
- Most cicada species produce exceptionally loud songs by the rapid buckling and unbuckling of drum-like structures known as tymbals.

### Tardigrades (Water Bear/Moss Piglet)

- Pages: 130
- Focus: Characteristics, survival mechanisms (cryptobiosis), and space experiments involving Tardigrades.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Eight-legged segmented micro-animals, also known as Water Bears or Moss Piglets.
- Endure extreme hot/cold temperatures, crushing pressures, and radiation through cryptobiosis.
- Cryptobiosis is a state of extreme inactivity in response to adverse environmental conditions.
- Being taken to the International Space Station (ISS) for experiments by Indian astronaut Shubhanshu Shukla.

#### Section Excerpt

Indian astronaut Shubhanshu Shukla will take Tardigrades to the International Space Station (ISS) for an experiment. Also known as Water Bears or Moss Piglets, these half-millimetre long, eight-legged segmented micro-animals endure extreme temperatures, crushing pressures, and radiation through cryptobiosis. Cryptobiosis is a state of extreme inactivity in response to adverse environmental conditions. Recognized classes include Eutardigrada and Heterotardigrada.

#### Claims

- Tardigrades are eight-legged segmented micro-animals commonly known as Water Bears or Moss Piglets.
- Tardigrades endure extreme temperatures, pressures, and radiation through cryptobiosis, which is a state of extreme inactivity.
- Recognized classes of Tardigrades include Eutardigrada and Heterotardigrada.
- Tardigrades are being taken to the International Space Station (ISS) for experiments by Indian astronaut Shubhanshu Shukla.

### Banana Musa Indandamanensis

- Pages: 131-132
- Focus: Discovery, physical characteristics, and genetic significance of the wild banana species Musa indandamanensis.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- Discovered in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands in 2012.
- Has the longest recorded infructescence in bananas at about 4.2 metres.
- Grows up to 11 metres high and features unique green flowers.
- Acts as a natural genetic resource for developing disease-resistant plant varieties.

#### Section Excerpt

An infructescence of about 4.2 metres recorded in species of wild banana Musa indandamanensis, making it the longest infructescence recorded in bananas. First recorded from a remote tropical forest near Krishna Nala reserve forest in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands in 2012. Unique green flowers; fruit bunch lux (axis) thrice size of regular banana species. 11 metres high. Natural genetic resource for plant breeders to develop high yielding and disease resistant varieties.

#### Claims

- Musa indandamanensis is a species of wild banana discovered in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands.
- Musa indandamanensis has the longest recorded infructescence among banana species, measuring about 4.2 metres.
- The Musa indandamanensis plant grows up to 11 metres high and features unique green flowers.
- Musa indandamanensis serves as a natural genetic resource for developing high-yielding and disease-resistant banana varieties.

Has 2 species: One native to coastal areas of tropical America, and parts of West Africa. Other found in arid coastal zones of Somalia and Yemen... Ornamental plant provides green canopy... Invasive (also known as green desert); excessive groundwater consumption; as allergenic pollen, etc.

#### Claims

- Conocarpus trees have been banned by the states of Gujarat and Tamil Nadu, and a government panel has recommended a Supreme Court ban.
- Conocarpus is not native to India; its species are native to coastal areas of tropical America, Africa, and the Arabian Peninsula.
- Conocarpus is an invasive ornamental plant often referred to as a 'green desert' due to its excessive groundwater consumption and production of allergenic pollen.

### Senna Spectabilis

- Pages: 134
- Focus: Invasive characteristics and eradication efforts in Kerala.
- Question quota hint: 2
- Claim count: 4

#### Evidence Bullets

- India's first science-based, community-driven eradication carried out in Wayanad, Kerala.
- Invasive species native to American tropicals.
- Forms dense thickets that choke native plants and alter soil chemistry.
- Resembles kanikkonna, the state flower of Kerala.

#### Section Excerpt

Kerala carried out India’s first science-based, community-driven eradication of Senna Spectabilis in Wayanad. Invasive species, Native to American tropicals. Forms dense, sterile thickets, choking out native plants, altering soil chemistry and depriving herbivores of food, grows 7-18m tall. Resembles Kerala’s state flower kanikkonna.

#### Claims

- Senna Spectabilis is an invasive plant species native to the American tropics.
- India's first science-based, community-driven eradication of Senna Spectabilis was carried out in Wayanad, Kerala.
- Senna Spectabilis forms dense, sterile thickets that choke out native plants, alter soil chemistry, and deprive herbivores of food.
- Senna Spectabilis visually resembles Kanikkonna, the state flower of Kerala.
